    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<a href="/questions/1430255-what-sort-of-age-groups-is-this-ok-for-i">What sort of age groups is this ok for? I work in a middle/high school and was wondering if it&#39;s ok for ages 12-13+.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1430255'><a id="like_count_community_question_1430255" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1430255?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F844422.Battle_Angel_Alita">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/91364648-jenni"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1579143512i/91364648._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/91364648-jenni">Jenni</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This series has some sexual themes and maybe a few nude moments, but very little, and not in the act of something sexual really. There is a lot of blo<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This series has some sexual themes and maybe a few nude moments, but very little, and not in the act of something sexual really. There is a lot of blood in some scenes, and very detailed body carnage. The main focus is on action and fighting for what's right, overcoming obstacles, and what it means to be human. The story can be very philosophical and empowering. Personally, I would let a group of mature 12-13+ kids read it, but some parents can be a bit more prudish. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4222688481026973441"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518238263ra/25034436.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I know I'm not the only one who saw the trailer for the movie that will be coming out this year and knew I had to get my hands on the source material. <br/><br/>I'm totally a newbie to graphic novels and manga. Aside from a brief obsession with Sailor Moon when I was a teenager, I'm woefully unfamiliar with all anime and under-read in all areas of manga. Picking up the Deluxe edition of <i>Battle Angel Alita</i> was sort of a leap of faith for me, but having read the first volume tonight I'm hopeful that this wi</span>
  <span id="freeText4222688481026973441" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518238263ra/25034436.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I know I'm not the only one who saw the trailer for the movie that will be coming out this year and knew I had to get my hands on the source material. <br><br>I'm totally a newbie to graphic novels and manga. Aside from a brief obsession with Sailor Moon when I was a teenager, I'm woefully unfamiliar with all anime and under-read in all areas of manga. Picking up the Deluxe edition of <i>Battle Angel Alita</i> was sort of a leap of faith for me, but having read the first volume tonight I'm hopeful that this will end up an unexpectedly pleasant surprise for me this month! <br><br>Volume 1, entitled <i>Rusty Angel</i> starts the reader off with a very, very soft introduction to the world as Alita is scavenged from a junkyard by a crafty repairman named Ido. This first volume seeks to introduce the readers only to the very surface of the world, the art style, and the characters. The scope of the world thus far remains centered around only what Alita is currently experiencing. She is a cypher through which the audience will continue to learn about the world.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518238263ra/25034437.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It makes for an extremely fast-paced read. It feels fresh and exciting, as there's really nothing to be confused by quite yet. The cover artwork for the volume definitely feels dated in comparison to some of the newer manga and comics I saw sitting on the shelf in the bookstore, but somehow it totally works here. It lends the story a gritty, retro feel that I'm totally into. <br><br>There's a definite focus on introducing elements of the story through action as well, which I personally think is the best way of delivering information about the world. Through a number of battle scenes and their consequences, we the reader learn about Alita's capabilities, and the abilities of a number of other cybertronic characters that exist in the world. Technology is definitely key here, and I truly enjoyed some of the ways it is implemented in the various action sequences. <br><br>Be wary though, this is definitely not for the faint of heart. There's a fair amount of gore in here, although frankly I think that's to be expected considering the title! My one qualm with this was that some of the dialogue felt a little stilted, especially in the second half, but otherwise I was totally invested.<br><br>Can't wait to see where the story goes next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4222688481026973441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_237857757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237857757" />
    <a title="Petros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6984857-petros"><img alt="Petros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321523871p2/6984857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237857757?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petros" href="/user/show/6984857-petros">Petros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237857757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3821026126392844751">Battle Angel Alita is the best manga I have read in my life (and I have read a lot). It has an amazing steampunk atmosphere, the artwork is very detailed, the attention to technology and the terminology they are using gives them an extra touch of realism, and the action scenes are epic and brutal.<br/><br/>Of course all that are just surface elements any shonentard could say to make even Black Clover to sound like a masterpiece, so let’s move to more substantial things. The protagonist is for me, by far t</span>
  <span id="freeText3821026126392844751" style="display:none">Battle Angel Alita is the best manga I have read in my life (and I have read a lot). It has an amazing steampunk atmosphere, the artwork is very detailed, the attention to technology and the terminology they are using gives them an extra touch of realism, and the action scenes are epic and brutal.<br /><br />Of course all that are just surface elements any shonentard could say to make even Black Clover to sound like a masterpiece, so let’s move to more substantial things. The protagonist is for me, by far the best female character in fiction. She is not defined by her gender or her sexuality, which is the case with almost every female character nowadays. She has a personality of her own, she is proactive, she is not dependent on men for feeling happy or secure, and above all, she constantly moves forward seeking more about who she is and what she wants in life. <br /><br />On a superficial level, the story is like a fighting shonen. Progressively stronger enemies appear, the protagonist is an underdog with amnesia that needs to power up and beat them for protecting her loved ones and eventually the world, before it’s revealed she was never an underdog and was special all along. The huge difference (which is also what makes it a seinen by the way) is how every conflict is mostly internal instead of external. Every challenge she faces is always related to how she thinks and feels; it’s not some generic one-dimensional villain who wants to take over the world for the heck of it. Overcoming a challenge is never about punching the bad guy harder than before; it’s about facing your fears and doubts. Hear that, D.Gray Man, you piece of shit?<br /><br />Another great thing about it is how it’s an actual subversion of typical superhero and fighting shonen stories. The term has lost its meaning these days, since people are using it for everything, but this manga is the purest form of it. Every arc starts in a cheesy way, it has a twist that flips around everything you assumed about it, it ends in a way that feels cathartic, and leads to legit character development. It’s not a satire that treats twists as a joke (One Punch Man), it’s not trying to be different for the sake of being different without actually doing something with it (The Force Awakens), and it definitely gives you much more than what you initially expected out of the premise (Black Clover). <br /><br />And I have to point out how it has a great plot progression with reasonable threat escalation and never collapses because of power creep. Getting stronger does not mean something superficial such as your hair having a different color, or your aura is bigger (Dragonball Super). The conflicts escalate in volume as they do in importance, beginning from backstreet psychotic killers and go all the way up to demigods that control the solar system. Their motives are not the same generic rule or kill everything, regardless of how strong they are. <br /><br />The more influence someone has because of his abilities, drastically changes his responsibilities and motives, which is why the petty street thug does not behave or think the same way as a demigod, so even the psychological conflicts gradually change from petty ones to bigger than life cosmological debates. And this is something I keep hearing a lot of people disliking about later arcs, especially in the Last Order sequel. A big part of the story is no longer about Alita, it’s about the world around Alita, which makes her feel distant and less relatable because of it. Even though that is the whole point of her plot progression; gradually becoming less selfish and more interested in existentialism issues that reach a cosmic level. <br /><br />Many complaints have also been said about the fighting tournament that takes place in Last Order. A huge part of it shows us what the other characters are doing instead of focusing on Alita all the time. Which is a completely dumb thing to say since that is exactly what made The Zenith of Things the best fighting tournament in fiction. In comparison to the Tournament of Power in Dragonball, which was just Goku and Vegeta steamrolling dozens of nobodies, and the sports festival of My Hero Academia, which was just a few boys screaming at each other with no tension whatsoever, ZOTT in comparison is a masterpiece. It bothers to flesh out most of the contestants, while offering world building at the same time, by showing us all the other places Alita never went to, and yet is supposed to be affecting with her ever-growing powers. Entire universes have been wiped out in Dragonball Super and you don’t give a shit about them because you know nothing about them. How is this better to what ZOTT is doing, you fools? You treat the manga as a fighting shonen and just want to see Alita as a waifu that steamrolls everyone. You are missing the big picture.<br /><br />In conclusion, Battle Angel Alita is the best manga ever made, and retains its consistency throughout its duration. It was not ruined like Berserk after the Eclipse, it did not lose its plot density like Eden is an Endless World, and it did not mutate from a Parasyte imitation to flower symbolism about one-dimensional rapists (Tokyo Ghoul). As for the complaints about the bug eyes Alita has in the upcoming live action movie, Cameron, you fucking idiot, every child-like character looked like that in the manga because of the artstyle. You killed its appeal a year before the movie is out and you will only manage to make people to read the manga. Which is better than nothing I guess. At least this way a lot of people will realize what trash fighting shonen have become nowadays. Fuck modern, Alita is almost 30 years old by now and it wins. As all retro always does.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3821026126392844751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jen/The Tolkien Gal/ジェニファー" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4919283-jen-the-tolkien-gal"><img alt="Jen/The Tolkien Gal/ジェニファー" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545334105p2/4919283.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319352088?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen/The Tolkien Gal/ジェニファー" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen/The Tolkien Gal/ジェニファー" href="/user/show/4919283-jen-the-tolkien-gal">Jen/The Tolkien Gal/ジェニファー</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4919283-jen-the-tolkien-gal?shelf=netgalley-challenge">netgalley-challenge</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319352088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9034751172437459674"><i>This book was provided to me by NetGalley in exchange for an honest review</i><br/><br/>I'm continuously amazed by the haul of old manga that pops up on Netgalley. These manga have fallen out of recent memory. I am so glad that the publisher's have given reviewers the opportunity to experience these groundbreaking pieces of art that enrich the cyberpunk and dystopian genres - especially in a reading environment where the same dystopian concept is reused and regurgitated with minor changes. <br/><br/>A man named Ido fin</span>
  <span id="freeText9034751172437459674" style="display:none"><i>This book was provided to me by NetGalley in exchange for an honest review</i><br><br>I'm continuously amazed by the haul of old manga that pops up on Netgalley. These manga have fallen out of recent memory. I am so glad that the publisher's have given reviewers the opportunity to experience these groundbreaking pieces of art that enrich the cyberpunk and dystopian genres - especially in a reading environment where the same dystopian concept is reused and regurgitated with minor changes. <br><br>A man named Ido finds a battered cyborg woman and makes it his mission to restore her. She has no memory of her past. Ido decides to name her Alita. Ido becomes obsessed with taking Alita's scant frame and making her beautiful. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520697227i/25193172.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> Soon you find out that Ido isn't the sweet, bumbling idiot he seems. However, Alita is not the empty-headed and child-like grown woman she comes across as, either. Luckily, she escapes the popular trope of becoming the child in a woman's body that many female characters in fantasy (who are alien in some way) fall victim to. <s>Here's looking at you, Bright and Fifth Element</s><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520697227i/25193173.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Books with character development always hit a sweet spot for me. From very early on, Alita is faced with a terrifying dilemma <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ where she believes that Ido is killing people to make up the parts she needs to be mobile again. She knows that Ido has given her a second chance, but is disgusted by her suspicions that he may be a killer <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Alita is kind and innocent-looking, but does not take too kindly to pressure from Ido to conform to his ideas for her appearance and future. The conflict between Alita's devotion to Ido and her suffocation from being restrained by him is a major theme in the manga, and it is well-developed throughout. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520697227i/25193174._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I love about older manga is that character design is much more unique and detailed than in the latest manga and anime. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520697227i/25193175._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The character developments, characters' perceptions of others, the influence of their past on their present self, motives and conflicts are subtly but beautifully portrayed. A character with all of these is a well-rounded and great character. These are things that are frequently thrown aside and replaced by superficial characterisations that make a book fall flat.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520697227i/25193176._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are elements common in cyberpunk - bountyhunters, cybernetic surgeons and noir themes. Battle Ange Alita manages to combine these elements in a balanced manner while still forming new, interesting concepts. In Alita's world, cybernetic enhancements are something that everyone has, but it is never enough - just like money. Because of the importance of these enhancements, people steal and kill others for something as trivial as stronger arms or as dangerous as human mince-maker of an arm.<br><br>In this book, people battle against internal strife as well as cybernetically enhanced monsters. In this book, characters do not have conflict over the idea of having mechanical parts - instead they are in conflict over what it means to be human and to have to live with yourself despite your past (or lack thereof).<br><br>Edit: So I found out this manga is getting turned into a movie by none other than James Cameron. And so I was curious as to how he would portray the fierce but cute Alita. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520921100i/25204660._SX540_.jpg" alt="Image result for battle angel alita james cameron" width="670" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>....<br><br>Ye gods. Kill it with fire.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2389371422" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2389371422" />
    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604273386p2/64621419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2389371422?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis">Dennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35218586-battle-angel-alita-vol-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=graphic-novels-comics-manga">graphic-novels-comics-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2389371422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13047313979750580721">A pretty cool manga that doesn’t realize its full potential in this first volume.<br/><br/>A cybernetics doctor finds the remnants of a female cyborg in the scrapyard and decides to rebuild her. He manages to revive her but learns that she’s lost her memory. He names her Alita, after his deceased cat.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549800053i/27042654._SY540_.png' width='300' height='567' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>Alita, after seeming a little subservient and childlike at first, thankfully soon develops a mind of her own. Thus allowing for a nice dynamic between her and the Doc.<br/><br/>She also slowly remembers a few thing</span>
  <span id="freeText13047313979750580721" style="display:none">A pretty cool manga that doesn’t realize its full potential in this first volume.<br><br>A cybernetics doctor finds the remnants of a female cyborg in the scrapyard and decides to rebuild her. He manages to revive her but learns that she’s lost her memory. He names her Alita, after his deceased cat.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549800053i/27042654._SY540_.png" width="300" height="567" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Alita, after seeming a little subservient and childlike at first, thankfully soon develops a mind of her own. Thus allowing for a nice dynamic between her and the Doc.<br><br>She also slowly remembers a few things of her past and subsequently decides to become a hunter-warrior. Someone who hunts down and kills cyber criminals.<br><br>And she’s immediately gunning for the big guys.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549800053i/27042655._SX540_.png" width="400" height="168" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The unfolding plot is a little minimalistic. But this manga looks very cool and has a kick-ass heroine to boot. To see her finding her strength over the course of this volume was very enjoyable.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549800053i/27042656._SY540_.png" width="400" height="585" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And she really has to as well, as she’s facing a powerful enemy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549800053i/27042657._SX540_.png" width="400" height="227" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately the final confrontation was a bit of a letdown.<br><br>But this manga certainly got a lot of style and a main character who’s story I definitely want to follow.<br><br>I’m looking forward to the next volume.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549800053i/27042658._SY540_.png" width="400" height="515" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13047313979750580721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3533982335" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3533982335" />
    <a title="David S Meanderings)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37021348-david-s-meanderings"><img alt="David S Meanderings)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580533662p2/37021348.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3533982335?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David S Meanderings)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David S Meanderings)" href="/user/show/37021348-david-s-meanderings">David S Meanderings)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35218586-battle-angel-alita-vol-1">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3533982335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7846397744638475791"><b>Review for both Volume 1 and 2</b><br/><br/>4.5 stars.<br/><br/>After rewatching the Alita: Battle Angel movie recently and remembering how much I love it, I knew I wanted to finally check out the manga that inspired it. I really loved this story that was darker and more twisted than the movie.<br/><br/>I was really surprised at how much I enjoyed the art in this manga. I tend to struggle feeling invested in the action in manga because it is hard for me to follow and fill in the blanks between panels. However, I thought that the</span>
  <span id="freeText7846397744638475791" style="display:none"><b>Review for both Volume 1 and 2</b><br /><br />4.5 stars.<br /><br />After rewatching the Alita: Battle Angel movie recently and remembering how much I love it, I knew I wanted to finally check out the manga that inspired it. I really loved this story that was darker and more twisted than the movie.<br /><br />I was really surprised at how much I enjoyed the art in this manga. I tend to struggle feeling invested in the action in manga because it is hard for me to follow and fill in the blanks between panels. However, I thought that the action in these volumes was very well done. It was easy to follow what was happening even in the action scene panels and the action felt fast paced and had high stakes.<br /><br />Alita is a compelling protagonist to follow. She is innnocent, yet ruthless. She is often introspective, but confident in making decisions and quick to act. She is kind hearted and trusting. She is also one of the most BA heroines that I have ever read about. It was such a joy to follow such a complex character.<br /><br /><i>“I don’t know if it’s a sin, or something to be proud of. I don’t know if it’s hate or mourning…All I know is that my tears flowed for him.”</i><br /><br />I often have trouble connecting with characters in manga because the medium itself limits the amount of words used and therefore can limit the author’s ability to dive deep into a character’s personality, motivations, etc. However, with Alita this was not the case. I instantly felt a connection with her honest, wild eyed, hope filled outlook on life even in the midst of the dark and grim reality of the world. Alita is truly just a good person. She wants to do her best by everybody she meets and contantly gives those she is fighting a chance to give up and surrender. I really love her character.<br /><br />The world itself is incredibly well done and immersive. Every panel felt intentional and added to the story or worldbuilding. I love the cyberpunk feel to this world. This is my first cyberpunk type story and I can tell you that I really enjoy it and will now be seeking out more stories that are set in this type of world.<br /><br />This is the first manga that I feel like I have gotten invested in for itself and not just because I have watched an adaptation previously. Surprisingly deep and meaningful, this is a story of hope in the darkness and of doing the right thing at all times no matter the consequence. I am really enjoying my journey through the Battle Angel Alita manga and will be continuing the series immediately!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7846397744638475791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35218586-battle-angel-alita-vol-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25276499-lexxi-kitty?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25276499-lexxi-kitty?shelf=format-manga">format-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25276499-lexxi-kitty?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25276499-lexxi-kitty?shelf=genre-science-fiction">genre-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25276499-lexxi-kitty?shelf=02-x-and-three-4ths-stars">02-x-and-three-4ths-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2316982533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7291886204735305256"><i>*I received this book from Kodansha Comics and Netgalley for an honest review*</i><br/><br/>Right, so - this is a futuristic world . . . . and um. hmms. I've no real idea what this world is. I don't even know if it takes place on earth. There's this junkyard the main male character lives in, and that the main female character was found in (without her memory). There's something floating in the sky that was called 'utopia', but beyond that I know nothing. Well, not nothing, obviously, not after reading this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText7291886204735305256" style="display:none"><i>*I received this book from Kodansha Comics and Netgalley for an honest review*</i><br /><br />Right, so - this is a futuristic world . . . . and um. hmms. I've no real idea what this world is. I don't even know if it takes place on earth. There's this junkyard the main male character lives in, and that the main female character was found in (without her memory). There's something floating in the sky that was called 'utopia', but beyond that I know nothing. Well, not nothing, obviously, not after reading this book. But I mean I don't know much about the setting - the world the book inhabits.<br /><br />I kind of despise the man. 'I would gladly feel their blood on my face! And in exchange I need you to be as pristine as my dream for you!' - so said the man; to which the woman/cyborg responded 'I'm not your dress-up doll!' - to which I applaud. Mildly.<br /><br />'I keep hunting for the pleasure'<br /><br />Wow this is one bloody gore filled manga. Really really bloody/gorey - it seems like . . . what's that called, blood porn? Gore porn? Something like that. <br /><br />Also one in which I didn't really understand what was going on 45 percent of the time. <br /><br /><br />This was a very violent, very weird story. I can't imagine it being turned into a movie, like the book description on Netgalley noted ('James Cameron is currently producing a live-action adaptation'). Considering the story, and what happens in it, making a live-action film will probably end up looking like that Film franchise 'Pacific Rim'. <br /><br />Right, so - that's read. The first volume, at least. I do not currently plan to continue the series. This just wasn't my type of thing.<br /><br />Rating: 2.78<br /><br />March 7 2018</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1936295557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12564096838218661125"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490241981i/22293961.jpg' width='336' height='353' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>4.5* For the series.<br/><br/>It took the first few arcs to get my bearings about where the story was going early on - I was worried that it was stagnating! But no, it just got better and better up until the end and I thoroughly enjoyed my time reading. The illustrations were simply gorgeous, characters memorable and the story was emotionally gripping and pleasantly unpredictable. Plenty of classic sci-fi ideas come into play but were all skilfully handled. I'd recommend this manga to anyone who enjoys sc</span>
  <span id="freeText12564096838218661125" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490241981i/22293961.jpg" width="336" height="353" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>4.5* For the series.<br><br>It took the first few arcs to get my bearings about where the story was going early on - I was worried that it was stagnating! But no, it just got better and better up until the end and I thoroughly enjoyed my time reading. The illustrations were simply gorgeous, characters memorable and the story was emotionally gripping and pleasantly unpredictable. Plenty of classic sci-fi ideas come into play but were all skilfully handled. I'd recommend this manga to anyone who enjoys scifi/dystopia, a good cry and a decent dose of action with a badass and iconic female protagonist.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=viz">viz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120529224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6384857762995732663">Well this book was certainly interesting though I had some issues with it for sure.<br/><br/>What's it about?<br/>A guy finds a scrappy robot with AI and after some repairs are done it turns out the robot is really powerful and good at fighting so she decides to become a warrior bot.<br/><br/>Pros:<br/>The story is very interesting.<br/>The art... I wasn't too sure at first but now I can say I definitely like it.<br/>The action scenes are very exciting and well done.<br/>The characters are interesting. The main character (Alita) is a reall</span>
  <span id="freeText6384857762995732663" style="display:none">Well this book was certainly interesting though I had some issues with it for sure.<br /><br />What's it about?<br />A guy finds a scrappy robot with AI and after some repairs are done it turns out the robot is really powerful and good at fighting so she decides to become a warrior bot.<br /><br />Pros:<br />The story is very interesting.<br />The art... I wasn't too sure at first but now I can say I definitely like it.<br />The action scenes are very exciting and well done.<br />The characters are interesting. The main character (Alita) is a really cool robotic bad-a** who never gives up and she is a really cool character!<br />The dog is a nice touch. I love doggies so much! 🐶<br /><br />Cons:<br />It's a bit predictable to be honest.<br />A lot of it's very cheesy, especially the main villain. He's meant to be intimidating but he's really the kind of thing I'd expect from an old Saturday morning cartoon only more violent (which honestly could be done well but isn't, the author makes it way too serious). Unfortunately the thing that really ruins the book for me a bit is how cheesy Kishiro makes this potentially great story throughout the entire thing.<br />There's this random baby that's added just to add more peril and this baby is annoying. I will be perfectly honest: I do not like kids, I don't like having to deal with (or even hear screaming from) kids in public places (example: the library) and I plan on never having kids (since I'm still a teenager some people tell me that I might change my mind but considering I have a literal list of reasons and would be willing to let a doctor use sharp tools near my genitals to avoid it I highly doubt that) and I usually think a book goes downhill when a kid is added to the story with a few exceptions (being East of West, Jennifer Blood, Roughneck and The Underwater Welder) and this is no exception. It's just annoying and to make it worse there's these f***ing crying baby sound effects and that sucks for people like me who hear dialogue and sound effects in their head while reading (though not in a weird voices in my head way) so that freaking sucked. (I will give it this, there's a great scene where the dog's told to take care of the baby and the dog makes a "urf werff" sound with a slightly sad look on it's face, that would definitely be me XD)<br />Some bits of the story were not well executed and not as clear as I would have liked them to be though I'm pretty sure I mostly understood it.<br /><br />Overall:<br />I kinda enjoyed it but it's not done very well at the same time. The art is good. The story, action and main character are freaking great! It's just I had major problems, mostly how cheesy they made this book. I don't think I'm bothered to continue reading this series especially since this volume works as a stand alone story but it's not bad if you were looking to give it a try.<br /><br />3/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="6384857762995732663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9206875592632103640">Earlier this month I saw <i>Alita: Battle Angel</i> at the movie theater and it was pretty cool to see on the big screen. The visuals are sleek and the world-building that we get is quite interesting, but there was so much more I wanted to know. That's why I decided to try the original manga to see how they compare.   <span id="freeText9206875592632103640" style="display:none">Earlier this month I saw <i>Alita: Battle Angel</i> at the movie theater and it was pretty cool to see on the big screen. The visuals are sleek and the world-building that we get is quite interesting, but there was so much more I wanted to know. That's why I decided to try the original manga to see how they compare. Now that I've read the first volume of the manga, I think I can say that I think I enjoyed the movie adaptation a little more in the long run. Most of that is because I felt like I was missing something right from the start. We barely get a taste of the surface of the world and characters that some things like character decision making skills and the world itself don't make much sense. It's probably a good thing I saw the movie first actually. I haven't decided if I want to continue on with the manga or the anime, yet.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522251521ra/25285660.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>

Some of the art was muddled to me, and it was difficult who was where and doing what, particularly in the fight scenes. That all said, I'm fascinated by this world and this character. I love the relationship between Alita and Ido and I want to keep reading to see where it goes, in case we don't get that Alita sequel...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9930252258425215969">I read most of this series back when Viz first published it in the traditional western comic book form in the 1990s, and I've had these collected editions on my shelf for years, but I'm only just rereading it for the first time. (I figured I'd refresh my memory before the new movie comes out.) This has some very nice art, though it's a little hard to "read" at times in this reduced size. There isn't much to the story apart from Alita's revival and her ongoing battle with the notorious brain-eati</span>
  <span id="freeText9930252258425215969" style="display:none">I read most of this series back when Viz first published it in the traditional western comic book form in the 1990s, and I've had these collected editions on my shelf for years, but I'm only just rereading it for the first time. (I figured I'd refresh my memory before the new movie comes out.) This has some very nice art, though it's a little hard to "read" at times in this reduced size. There isn't much to the story apart from Alita's revival and her ongoing battle with the notorious brain-eating cyborg Makaku, whose character is quite over-the-top. If I remember correctly, there's more character development to balance the action in subsequent volumes.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3395287115" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10478762587776902921"><b>3.5/5 stars</b><br/><br/>Battle Angel Alita takes place in a dystopian cyberpunk world, where Ido, a cybernetics doctor finds a broken and amnesiac cyborg in a junkyard, who he names Alita, and rebuilds her.<br/><br/>The characters are yet to be fleshed out, and the villain of this arc feels very superficial so far, but the plot, action and overall setting keeps the readers intrigued. The manga is also gorgeously drawn, so detailed and beautiful.<br/><br/>A must read for fans of sci-fi and cyberpunk.</span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer483504492" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16276699756588648886">easily in the top 5 sci-fi manga series of all time (along w/ Ghost in the Shell, Appleseed, and Macross/Robotech) -- techno-punk at its best, featuring over-the-top cybernetic martial arts and gorgeously intricate artwork</span>

  <span id="freeText1316720914861558730" style="display:none">I will not stand by, in the presence of little reviews for this manga! So I am a massive fan of the new Alita Battle Angel film, as it's easily my favourite film of this year so far! So I'd thought I'd give the manga the movie is based on, a read and see if it's any good. <br /><br />First off I will say that the artwork is amazing and so well drawn! Some of the panels were even recreated directly in the movie which just makes me love it even more. And like the film, the action scenes are fantastic! In other respects, some of the characters are kind of brushed over and not developed all that much. The story often feels a little less coherent, compared to the film and OVA. Granted the manga is the original source material, but I just feel the anime and movie were able to take the story and tell it in a more coherent way that felt less scrambled. Otherwise, though this was a good first volume and I can't wait to read the next one!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35218586-battle-angel-alita-vol-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18907573-carol-flores?shelf=manga">manga</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3511990099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2894318661566843571"><b>Trigger warning: graphic and violent scenes. This should be read only by +18.</b><br/><br/><b>2.5/5</b><br/>I have mixed emotions about this, so I’m gonna try to explain myself:<br/><br/>First of all, it’s impossible not to compare the manga with the movie directed by Robert Rodriguez because it was the bomb when it came out and it still one of my fav movies from 2019.<br/><br/>That being said, I think both of them complement each other, because if I were only to read the manga, I think I wouldn’t even like the story at all. Please be aware</span>
  <span id="freeText2894318661566843571" style="display:none"><b>Trigger warning: graphic and violent scenes. This should be read only by +18.</b><br /><br /><b>2.5/5</b><br />I have mixed emotions about this, so I’m gonna try to explain myself:<br /><br />First of all, it’s impossible not to compare the manga with the movie directed by Robert Rodriguez because it was the bomb when it came out and it still one of my fav movies from 2019.<br /><br />That being said, I think both of them complement each other, because if I were only to read the manga, I think I wouldn’t even like the story at all. Please be aware that this is on my taste alone but, some of the reasons that made me rate this 3/5 are: <br /><br />-The manga is fast paced and though we have a bunch of action scenes, they don’t feel dynamic as I would have like to. And we only get glimpses of the dystopian world they live in. <br /><br />-Character development? What I mean with this is that Alita is a cyborg (?) that has all these powers and she knows how to fight right from the start, with no training whatsoever. She doesn’t have much charisma and ultimately, she’s not a relatable character nor someone I feel empathy for. At least, not with the first volume. <br /><br />-Ido and Alita have a thing, kind of. In the movie Ido is more a father-like character, but in here they have an ambiguous relationship that made me so uncomfortable, mostly because she’s just a kid and he’s a grown man. <br /><br />-Wasn’t a big fan of the art style. This was made +20 years ago, so if you’re really picky about that like me, this might not be your cup of tea either. Though I did like how characters are drawn different from each other. <br /><br />Now, like I said, I think both movie and manga complement each other well because in the movie we see a more ‘human’ Alita, we see her change and grow into a badass and likeable character. In the movie, we also explore the world a little bit more and it takes the time to explain what is this about.<br /><br />Unfortunately, with the manga everything is rushed. There’s still no explanation to why there is another ‘city’ above the scraps and we don’t really know who the big bad wolf is yet. <br /><br />If I’m being honest, I don’t know if I’ll be continuing with the series. At least, is not a priority of mine, so I might just end up DNF-ing the series. I’m still not sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2894318661566843571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_15226683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15226683" />
    <a title="Nick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/899659-nick"><img alt="Nick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1265642637p2/899659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15226683?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick" href="/user/show/899659-nick">Nick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781569319451" href="/book/show/1898943.Battle_Angel_Alita_Volume_1_Battle_Angel_Alita">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899659-nick?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15226683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16062473421014282896"><b>Overall Rating: A</b><br/><i>Synopsis: Battle Angel Alita tells the story of an amnesiac female cyborg named Alita. Alita's head and upper torso are found in a state of suspended animation by cybermedic/bounty hunter Daisuke Ido while he is searching for useful scrap. After giving her a new body, Alita begins to learn how to live in the Scrapyard, the home of the poor and out-of-luck, who live in the shadow of the floating city of Tiphares, where the rich live. Although she has no memory, Alita soon realize</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16062473421014282896" style="display:none"><b>Overall Rating: A</b><br /><i>Synopsis: Battle Angel Alita tells the story of an amnesiac female cyborg named Alita. Alita's head and upper torso are found in a state of suspended animation by cybermedic/bounty hunter Daisuke Ido while he is searching for useful scrap. After giving her a new body, Alita begins to learn how to live in the Scrapyard, the home of the poor and out-of-luck, who live in the shadow of the floating city of Tiphares, where the rich live. Although she has no memory, Alita soon realizes she knows the legendary Martian martial art, Panzer Kunst. The series follows Alita as she recovers her past and uncovers the secrets of Tiphares. </i><br /><br />My only complaint about <i>Battle Angel Alita</i> is that the story can get a little slow over the 9 volumes. Aside from that, there is a lot to love. For a series that was written in 1991, <i>Battle Angel Alita</i> holds up surprisingly well as a science fiction story. <br /><br />Set in a futuristic dystopian society, Alita shares the stage with some excellent supporting characters as well. Along with her father figure, Ido, there is Desty Nova, an insane nanotechnologist, and Kaos, Nova's son, a frail and troubled radio DJ with psychometric powers. These characters make Alita more interesting as a character as she struggles to retrieve her memory.<br /><br />I definitely recommend checking the series out if you're into Science Fiction. It may not be as much fun if you aren't a sci-fi nerd like me, but give a shot and see what you think. Battle Angel Alita is a classic manga that's worth trying.<br /><br />For more manga and anime reviews, please check out <a href="http://hobotaku.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Hobotaku</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16062473421014282896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2223396265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2223396265" />
    <a title="Jay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50432252-jay"><img alt="Jay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451592702p2/50432252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2223396265?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jay" href="/user/show/50432252-jay">Jay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35218586-battle-angel-alita-vol-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50432252-jay?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50432252-jay?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50432252-jay?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2223396265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12176215496075819960">A fun, violent take on Cyberpunk. I'm revisiting this series, in part, because of the upcoming film (the trailers have been awesome, and I love me some Robert Rodriguez), but also to see if it holds up for me, as it has been almost twenty years since I first picked this up.<br/>The writing is kinda meh; the plot is really just an excuse for fight scenes, the world (in this first volume) is barely sketched out, and the dialog is mostly serviceable but veers wildly from awful to pretty good from panel </span>
  <span id="freeText12176215496075819960" style="display:none">A fun, violent take on Cyberpunk. I'm revisiting this series, in part, because of the upcoming film (the trailers have been awesome, and I love me some Robert Rodriguez), but also to see if it holds up for me, as it has been almost twenty years since I first picked this up.<br />The writing is kinda meh; the plot is really just an excuse for fight scenes, the world (in this first volume) is barely sketched out, and the dialog is mostly serviceable but veers wildly from awful to pretty good from panel to panel. Really, the writing is there to hang the pretty pictures on.<br />What pictures, though! There is a definite Metal Hurlant influence in the backgrounds, which contrasts well with the trad-manga character designs. The combat scenes are brilliant and hugely creative, and some of this stuff is bonkers in the best possible way. It's gorgeous.<br />This is a fun ride that makes up for some lame scripting with spectacle. There are few graphic works, Eastern or Western, with as much visual razzmatazz as you find here, and that verve makes it easy to ignore some of the flaws. If you like Cyberpunk, epic robot battles, or pretty ultraviolence, look no further.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12176215496075819960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2291492814" />
    <a title="Wayne McCoy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4054541-wayne-mccoy"><img alt="Wayne McCoy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331517656p2/4054541.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2291492814?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wayne McCoy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wayne McCoy" href="/user/show/4054541-wayne-mccoy">Wayne McCoy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4054541-wayne-mccoy?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2291492814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1826411192884076559">'Battle Angel Alita, Volume 1: Rusty Angel' by Yukito Kishiro seems like a timely release with an upcoming movie coming out. It's also a really good read.<br/><br/>Daisuke Ido likes looking for cyborg parts in the junk heaps. When he finds the head of a cyborg, he rebuilds her into Alita. Alita has little memory of who she was before, but she knows she must fight. After a crushing defeat, she is rebuilt into an even fiercer weapon and goes out to get revenge on the scary Makaku.<br/><br/>It's definitely a classic s</span>
  <span id="freeText1826411192884076559" style="display:none">'Battle Angel Alita, Volume 1: Rusty Angel' by Yukito Kishiro seems like a timely release with an upcoming movie coming out. It's also a really good read.<br /><br />Daisuke Ido likes looking for cyborg parts in the junk heaps. When he finds the head of a cyborg, he rebuilds her into Alita. Alita has little memory of who she was before, but she knows she must fight. After a crushing defeat, she is rebuilt into an even fiercer weapon and goes out to get revenge on the scary Makaku.<br /><br />It's definitely a classic series with a deep dystopian SF feel. The world is populated, but it seems as if most people have been turned into partial cyborgs. <br /><br />The art is some of the best I've seen in manga and I loved the detail. Many of the chapters also included a few introductory color pages, and these were really well done. I'm glad I finally got to read a chapter in this classic series.<br /><br />I received a review copy of this manga from Kodansha Comics and NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you for allowing me to review this manga.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1826411192884076559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2698088771" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2698088771" />
    <a title="Tvrtko Balić" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24472414-tvrtko-bali"><img alt="Tvrtko Balić" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605273392p2/24472414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2698088771?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tvrtko Balić" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tvrtko Balić" href="/user/show/24472414-tvrtko-bali">Tvrtko Balić</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24472414-tvrtko-bali?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2698088771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3157516036188362146">If you are looking for a really fun cyberpunk manga, I would recommend this book. Alita is too much of a Mary Sue, but the plot is handled well enough. Also, it is extremely cheesy, but that can be a good or a bad thing (I'd say it lands on the good side). I was thinking about giving a three star rating, it seemed to fit perfectly a fun story and a great introduction to the characters and the world, but one that is also flawed and unclear of where it is going. But then the extra chapters at the </span>
  <span id="freeText3157516036188362146" style="display:none">If you are looking for a really fun cyberpunk manga, I would recommend this book. Alita is too much of a Mary Sue, but the plot is handled well enough. Also, it is extremely cheesy, but that can be a good or a bad thing (I'd say it lands on the good side). I was thinking about giving a three star rating, it seemed to fit perfectly a fun story and a great introduction to the characters and the world, but one that is also flawed and unclear of where it is going. But then the extra chapters at the end (I hope they are included in this edition) blew me away, there is definitely more good stuff coming from this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3157516036188362146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oewVue7Q9zUyydk1jxThWLJw27lYrYiOkwyuElwtcxvcHN2gXVaMbr6edfdDCulHrJ89JSeoViFTzqfJv7EcZQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F4u28B5pGzb5JBFAzit89d3SClcor6fiXZpimL8pPQ1qe37pre9gbXVzvYICNXTqwz3sy1eqeU2dWGtDXLVScw==')})
  }
